All Reviews

  1. What can I say about this item? Hmmm. It's created such a craze but after a months use I still haven't found it to be a NECESSITY in your makeup stash.<br /><br />Regardless of the claims, I've found that the beauty blender eats product. If you're using expensive items, this is not cost efficient in terms of use. My hands down favorite use for this is to apply loose powder and I've even quickly gone through a quarter of that when one bottle typically lasts me 6 months. I've noticed with liquid products, it's best to apply on your face and blend with BB. I've seen tutorials apply directly to the BB and in all my experiments the BB eats up some of the product. Period.<br /><br />The larger issue that I have is the fact that I like a med-full coverage look. I've found that the BB thins out product to look a step down from what it should (med cov items look like light cov and so forth). While for some it may allow for a &#34;natural&#34; look, I prefer my product not to be sheered out as it causes unnecessary layers to get medium/full coverage effect.<br /><br />What I DO like about this product is for use for MUA's or other professionals. It's used wet and easy to clean after each client with access to water terminal of some sort. As I mentioned above, it's done the best job at applying powder products for me by leaving a smooth and silky finish instead of a chalky looking one. The shape of it is also great, it allows you to use various angles to target large, small or hard to get to areas.<br /><br />As for the cleanser, I like it but I can't say that it would make a huge difference than using something gentle like baby wash. Stains can be hard to remove but usually come out well with VERY hot water. I've also found that it's best to clean when it's dry and start by massaging in the cleanser or the dry BB before adding water and massaging to clean. It's also important to note to be considerably gentle. I softly went in with the front of my nail to try and force out astain and noticed a small rip in it the next day. Recommended to clean with massaging only fingertips.<br /><br />All in all I see this as a great product for those who are professionals or everyday people who enjoy a light natural coverage with very little effort. Contour queens may enjoy using this as well to blend in harsh lines.<br /><br />At this point, I probably wouldn't personally repurchase without trying a cheaper generic version. For me, the BB fails to live up to its hype.

  30. This is my first review, but I was so pleasantly surprised by how well this product works that I had to leave some feedback. After having perfect skin for years, my face suddenly went berserk on me in my mid-twenties and nothing I've tried has stopped the breakouts or scarring. So I've been forced to become a major makeup consumer and I'm always on the lookout for anything to make my life easier in the makeup department. I prefer mineral makeup to liquid, and the only way I've found to get adequate coverage is to start with a thick creme concealer (like dermablend) on the blemishes, then go over my whole face with a mineral foundation. Unfortunately this often results in a yucky pancake effect over the concealed areas, and achieving even looking coverage is a real pain. But it's still the best method I've found so far, since an all creme/liquid approach leaves me looking like a geisha and the all mineral \\"buffing\\" action tends to buff away any concealing effect and defeat the purpose. So you can see why I'm always on the lookout for anything that might help. Also it is a pain in the butt to keep all of those brushes clean. So after trying just about all of the brushes on the market I turned to these sponges out of curiosity. I had high hopes but low expectations, as they seemed pretty gimmicky. But desperate times call for desperate measures, and I figured that even if the sponges were crap that I could use the cleaner on my huge brush collection. Even though they seemed like they would only be good to use with liquid foundation, I decided to try using them with the mineral foundation first just for the heck of it. Dampened the sponge as suggested (it bloated up rather alarmingly) and sat down at the makeup table expecting a steep learning curve. First I used the pointy end to apply and blend the creme concealer with surprisingly good results. I did have to go over one or two of the darker spots with a small brush, but using the \\"stippling\\" motion to blend everything worked well without sacrificing coverage. So far so good. Now for the moment of truth-applying the powder foundation. Usually this involves several minutes of patting, gentle buffing, blending, patting again to replace the coverage that was lost from the buffing, etc. Not with this baby. It took maybe a minute of \\"stippling\\" to get an even, non-cakey finish. I probably used half as much product as usual, and there wasn't a huge powdery mess on the table. Pretty shocking. I couldn't believe it was that easy, so I went to check it out in a variety of different lighting, convinced that there must be some streak or blob somewhere that needed fixing. Nope, looks great. I was sold, even used the pointy end to clean up an eye makeup oops without messing up my foundation. I was ready to post this review then and there, but decided to try out the cleanser first so I could include it. I don't know what the complaints are about, the dispenser worked fine and the sponge cleaned up easily. The lavender smell is a bonus, very nice. Part of the reason it was so easy to clean is that the sponge absorbed almost no product, so everything was just on the surface. Of course I only tried it with powder, it may soak up more liquid foundation. It seems designed to keep the product on the outside, so you don't lose as much foundation (and $$$) by having it sucked into a sponge. Sorry this review is so long (and probably boring), but when you've tried as many different (and almost invariably disappointing) types of makeup and applicators as I have it always comes as a shock to find a product that works as well as it says it does. EDIT 2/18/12 I figured out how to get the beauty blender completely clean! I've been doing this for about a month now, and it consistently cleans the blender perfectly. Instead of washing after use, I let it dry dirty and wash right before use. Put the cleaner on the sponge while it's dry, and rub it in with your hands. Then, under warm water, just splash a tiny bit of water on it, and work it in. Then, get it real nice and soaked and get all the soap out and all the color should come out and your sponge will look like new again!

  118. Awesome Price for 2 beauty blenders and a cleanser!<br /><br />I've only tried the blenders twice so far, and both times I've loved the results. My BB and CC creams go on great; even better results than my real techniques brush. The difference is &#34;stamping&#34; your foundation/creams with the blender, vs &#34;swirling&#34; with a brush. I tried to use the blender with a setting powder, but prefer to use a brush for setting powders from now on and use the blenders just for cream products. If you've never used a beauty blender before, you should wet it and then towel dry before applying product. The blender will grow in size and be a little damp, but works best this way. You should wash your blenders regularly. I wash mine after each application, but I have friends who wash it every 2 applications. The first few times you wash the blender pink dye runs out in the water, but no pink dye is ever transferred from the blender to your makeup/skin.<br /><br />I wasn't very impressed with the liquid cleanser or the dispenser. To use the dispenser you're supposed to push the blender onto the top, but the liquid doesn't really get absorbed and ends up squirting down the side of the bottle. I also had to use a lot of product and it didn't get all the cream off. I ended up washing the blender 3 times, then used my regular brush cleanser to get everything completely off. Make sure to let the blender air dry completely (the package has a clear plastic stand to use), or else the blender can and will grow mold (friend's experience).<br /><br />Overall, I loved the blenders, but wasn't impressed with the cleanser. However, you can't beat this price! Amazon's price for this package at the time I purchased it was $30.99, and Sephora's price is 39.95!

It looks like you are not wearing any foundation, even if you have to use a heavy concealer. Just be sure to dampen the sponge per the instructions. On the days when I'm in a rush and decide to mayyybe blend a little with my fingers, I can instantly tell the difference and immediately go back to the sponge.<br /><br />- The sponge's shape is easy to use: you can cover large areas fast + get into small delicate areas, like under the eyes.<br /><br />- You can blend with multiple foundation shades to your heart's content (i.e. darker on your nose and lighter around the jaw line). I've also used multiple foundation weights: sheer, regular, and heavy concealer.<br /><br />- You can have sheer coverage, or heavy coverage, by how much you dab.<br /><br />- I loooove how the cleanser smells.<br /><br />CONS<br /><br />- You will use a lot more foundation. It doesn't lather well either.<br /><br />- Makeup and pink dye will coat your sink when you clean the sponges. A spray bottle with 50% water / 50% vinegar takes it off in a flash.<br /><br />- The cleanser dispenser isn't very functional. One \\"swoosh\\" of the sponge in the basin, per the instructions, is never enough to clean the sponge. However, I love the smell of the cleanser so much that I keep buying it.
